(10) The visitation fee for issuing Letter of Intent, Letter of Permission, Letter of Renewal of Permission in
connection with establishment of new college or institution and for increase number of seats shall be paid as given
below by way of a Demand Draft or Online Payment (National Electronic Funds Transfer or Real Time Gross
Settlement) as specified by the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine in favour of
‘the National Commission Fund for Indian System of Medicine’ New Delhi along with all applicable taxes,-
(i) Visitation fee: Rupees one lakh (per visitation);
(ii) Digitisation fee: Rupees thirty thousand (per visitation).

13. Phase-Wise Establishments of New Colleges or Institutions and Requirements of Minimum Essential
Standards.- Sowa-Rigpa colleges, permitted for starting Menpa Kachupa (Bachelor of Sowa-Rigpa Medicine and
Surgery) course under section 29 of the Act, shall establish infrastructure, facilities, and manpower phase-wise,
namely,-

[भाग III—खण् ड 4] भारत का रािपत्र : असाधारण 77
(1) Before admission of the first batch of students, the college or institution shall fulfill the minimum
essential standard requirements of the first phase of establishment namely.- (a) at the time of submission of
application, there shall be a fully developed hospital building in the proposed land as specified in sub-regulation
(1) and (2) of regulation 4 with fully-functional and registered Sowa-Rigpa hospital, existing not less than one year
prior to the date of application as specified in the clause (b) of sub-regulation (1) of regulation 10, having
appropriate number of beds, bed occupancy and out-patient attendance corresponding to the annual students intake
capacity as specified in clause (b) of sub-regulation (4) under regulation 4 and sub-regulation (1) of regulation 6;
(b) all teachers as specified in sub-regulation (2) under regulation 5 with the requisite qualification as
mentioned in the National Commission for Indian System of Medicine (Minimum Standards of Undergraduate
Sowa-Rigpa Education Regulations, 2022) and non-teaching staff as specified in sub-regulation (3) under
regulation 5 which are required for first professional session of teaching and training shall be appointed;
(c) (i) minimum one specialist doctor or clinical teacher with requisite qualifications in each of the two
combined out-patient departments [1. combined department of lus nad (General Medicine) and gdon nad dang
dug nad (Clinical Psychology and Toxicology) and 2. combined department of dpyad sbyong (External
Therapy and Surgery) and byis nad dang mo nad (Paediatrics and Gynaecology)] shall be appointed;
(ii) the experience of specialist doctor or clinical teacher shall be considered as a teacher from the date of
appointment of the specialist doctor or clinical teacher or one year prior to the submission of application by
the applicant to the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine to establish a
college or institution whichever is lesser;
(d) External therapy section and Minor Operation Theatre, Clinical laboratory as mentioned in Schedule-I,
Schedule-X and Schedule-XI; and instruments and equipment in Out- Patient Department and In-Patient
Department as per the Schedule- XII;
(e) a library with two thousand five hundred books with fifteen seating capacity for up to fifteen students intake
capacity and a library with twenty-five seating capacity for sixteen to thirty students intake capacity and staff
as specified in Schedule-VI;
(f) well-equipped and furnished two lecture halls or classrooms, teaching departments attached with laboratory,
museum and other ancillary units or sections as applicable (i.e., dissection hall, anatomy museum, physiology
laboratory, language laboratory, pathology laboratory) for the first professional session of teaching and training
with all infrastructure, facilities, manpower as specified in Schedules-I to XIII as applicable and shall have
Medical Education Unit as per the clause (i) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4 and Information Technology
Support and Communication facilities as per the clause (h) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4;
(g) there shall be a Teaching Pharmacy and Quality Testing Laboratory and Materia Medica Museum attached
to Department of sman rdzas dang sman sbyor (Materia Medica, Pharmacology and Pharmaceutics) with
minimum area as specified in Schedule–II, equipment or instruments as specified in Schedule-IX and
specimens in the Materia Medica Museum as per Schedule-XIII;
(h) an herbal garden covering over one thousand square meter of land and one thousand five hundred square
meters of land for admission up to fifteen seats and sixteen to thirty seats respectively as per Schedule-III with
plantation of minimum thirty species of medicinal plants and staff as mentioned in Schedule-VI;
(i) all the hospital staff shall be as specified in Schedule-IV; and
(j) there shall be a biometric attendance system supported with web camera based computerised attendance
system for teaching staff, non-teaching college staff and hospital staff.
(2) Before admission of second batch of the students, the college or institution shall fulfill or maintain the
minimum essential standard requirements of the second phase of establishment, namely:- (a) there shall be a
functional Sowa-Rigpa hospital having appropriate number of beds, bed occupancy and out-patient attendance
corresponding to the annual students intake capacity as specified clause (b) of sub-regulation (4) under regulation
4 and sub-regulation (1) of regulation 6;
(b) all teachers as specified in sub-regulation (2) under regulation 5 with the requisite qualification as
mentioned in the National Commission for Indian System of Medicine (Minimum Standards of Undergraduate
Sowa-Rigpa Education Regulations, 2022) and non-teaching staff as specified in sub-regulation (3) under
regulation 5, which are required for the first and the second professional sessions of teaching and training;
(c) minimum one specialist doctor or one clinical teacher with requisite mandatory qualifications in each of the
two combined out-patient departments [(1. combined department of lus nad (General Medicine) and gdon nad
dang dug nad (Clinical Psychology and Toxicology) and 2. combined department of dpyad sbyong (External
Therapy and Surgery) and byis nad dang mo nad (Paediatrics and Gynaecology)];

78 THE GAZETTE OF INDIA : EXTRAORDINARY [PART III—SEC.4]
(d) External therapy section and Minor Operation Theatre, Clinical laboratory as mentioned in Schedule-I and
facilities as per the Schedule-X and XI; and instruments and equipment in Out- Patient Department and In-
Patient Department as per the Schedule- XII;
(e) a library with three thousand books with twenty seating capacity for up to fifteen students intake capacity
and a library with forty seating capacity for sixteen to thirty students intake capacity and staff as specified in
Schedule-VI;
(f) well-equipped and furnished three lecture halls or class rooms, teaching departments, attached with
laboratories, museum and other ancillary units or sections as applicable (i.e., dissection hall, anatomy museum,
physiology laboratory, language laboratory, pathology laboratory) for first and second professional session of
teaching and training with all infrastructure, facilities, man power as specified in Schedules-I to XIII as
applicable and shall have Medical Education Unit as per the clause (i) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4,
Information Technology support and communication facilities as per the clause (h) sub-regulation (5) of
regulation 4 and Clinical Skill Laboratory as per the clause (d) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4;
(g) there shall be a Teaching pharmacy and Quality Testing Laboratory and Materia Medica Museum attached
to Department of sman rdzas dang sman sbyor (Materia Medica, Pharmacology and Pharmaceutics) with
minimum area as specified in Schedule-II, equipment or instruments as specified in Schedule-IX and
specimens in the Materia medica museum as per Schedule-XIII;
(h) an herbal garden covering over one thousand square meter of land and one thousand five hundred square
meters of land for admission up to fifteen seats and sixteen to thirty seats respectively as per Schedule–III with
plantation of minimum forty species of medicinal plants;
(i) all the hospital staff shall be as specified in Schedule-IV; and
(j) there shall be biometric attendance system supported with web camera based computerized attendance
system for teaching staff, non-teaching college staff and hospital staff.
(3) Before admission of third batch of students, the college or institution shall fulfil or maintain the
minimum essential standard requirements of the third phase of establishment as follow.- (a) there shall be a
functional Sowa-Rigpa hospital having appropriate number of beds, bed occupancy and out-patient attendance
corresponding to the annual students intake capacity as specified clause (b) of sub-regulation (4) under regulation
4 and sub-regulation (1) of regulation 6;
(b) all teachers as specified in sub-regulation (2) under regulation 5 with the requisite qualification as
mentioned in the concerned National Commission for Indian System of Medicine (Minimum Standards of
Undergraduate Sowa-Rigpa Education Regulations, 2022) and non-teaching staff as specified in sub-regulation
(3) under regulation 5, which are required for the first and the second professional sessions of teaching and
training;
(c) minimum one specialist doctor or one clinical teacher in each of the two combined Out-Patient Departments
[1. Combined department of lus nad (General Medicine) and gdon nad dang dug nad (Clinical Psychology and
Toxicology) and 2. Combined department of dpyad sbyong (External Therapy and Surgery) and byis nad dang
mo nad (Paediatrics and Gynaecology)];
(d) External therapy section and Minor Operation Theatre, Clinical laboratory as mentioned in Schedule-I and
facilities as per the Schedule-X and XI; and instruments and equipment in Out- Patient Department and In-
Patient Department as per the Schedule- XII;
(e) a library with three thousand five hundred books with twenty seating capacity for up to fifteen students
intake capacity and a library with forty seating capacity for sixteen to thirty students intake capacity and staff
as specified in Schedule-VI;
(f) well-equipped and furnished four lecture halls or class rooms, teaching departments, attached with
laboratories, museum and other ancillary units or sections as applicable (i.e., dissection hall, anatomy museum,
physiology laboratory, language laboratory, pathology laboratory) for first and second professional session of
teaching and training with all infrastructure, facilities, man power as specified in Schedule–I to XIII and shall
have Medical Education Unit as per the clause (i) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4, Information Technology
support and communication facilities as per the clause (h) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4 and Clinical Skill
Laboratory as per the clause (d) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4;
(g) Teaching pharmacy and Quality Testing Laboratory and Museum attached to Department of sman rdzas
dang sman sbyor (Materia Medica, Pharmacology and Pharmaceutics) with minimum area as specified in
Schedule-II, equipment or instruments as specified in Schedule-IX and specimens in the Materia medica
museum as per Schedule-XIII;

[भाग III—खण् ड 4] भारत का रािपत्र : असाधारण 79
(h) an herbal garden covering over one thousand square meter of land and one thousand five hundred square
meters of land for admission up to fifteen seats and sixteen to thirty seats respectively as per Schedule-III with
plantation of minimum fifty species of medicinal plants;
(i) all the hospital staff shall be as specified in Schedule-IV; and
(j) there shall be biometric attendance system supported with web camera based computerised attendance
system for teaching staff, non-teaching college staff and hospital staff.
(4) Before the commencement of fourth batch of students, the college or institution shall fulfil or maintain
the minimum essential standard requirements of the fourth (final) phase of establishment as follow.- (a)
there shall be a functional Sowa-Rigpa hospital with four independent Out-Patient Departments as specified in
clause (d) under sub-regulation (4) of regulation 4 having appropriate number of beds, bed occupancy and Out-
Patient Department attendance corresponding to the annual students intake capacity as specified in clause (b) of
sub-regulation (4) under regulation 4 and sub-regulation (1) of regulation 6;
(b) all teachers as specified in sub-regulation (2) under regulation 5 with the requisite qualification as
mentioned in the concerned NCISM regulations and non-teaching staff as specified in sub-regulation (3) under
regulation 5, which are required for the first, second and third professional session of teaching and training;
(c) all infrastructure, facilities and manpower requirements of college, hospital and other units in accordance
with as specified in these regulations 4 to 6 and Schedule-I to XIII;
(d) a library with four thousand books, seating capacity of thirty persons for admission up to fifteen student
intake capacity and seating capacity of fifty persons for sixteen to thirty student intake capacity and staff as
specified in Schedule-VI;
(e) well-equipped and furnished five lecture halls or class rooms, teaching departments, attached with
laboratories, museum and other ancillary units or sections as applicable (i.e., dissection hall, anatomy museum,
physiology laboratory, language laboratory, pathology laboratory), for first, second and third professional
session of teaching and training with all infrastructure, facilities, man power as specified in Schedules-I to XIII
and shall have shall have Medical Education Unit as per the clause (i) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4,
Information Technology support and communication facilities as per the clause (h) sub-regulation (5) of
regulation 4 and Clinical Skill Laboratory as per the clause (d) sub-regulation (5) of regulation 4;
(f) the Teaching pharmacy and Quality Testing Laboratory and Museum attached to Department of sman rdzas
dang sman sbyor (Materia Medica, Pharmacology and Pharmaceutics) with minimum area as specified in
Schedule-II, equipment or instruments as specified in Schedule-IX and specimens in the museum as per
Schedule-XIII;
(g) a fully developed herbal garden with minimum seventy species of medicinal plants as specified in
Schedule-III;
(h) assured round the clock availability of medical services including medicines, paramedical staff, doctors and
emergency management in the hospital; and
(i) there shall be biometric attendance system supported with web camera based computerised attendance
system for teaching staff, non-teaching college staff and hospital staff.
CHAPTER-V
RATING OF FULLY ESTABLISHED EXISTING SOWA-RIGPA MEDICAL COLLEGES OR
INSTITUTIONS UNDER SECTION 28 OF THE ACT
14. Rating of fully Established or Existing Sowa-Rigpa Colleges.- (1) The Medical Assessment and Rating Board
for Indian System of Medicine shall assess and rate the college or institution every year as per the procedure
determined by the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine in accordance with the key
areas and standards determined by the Board of Unani, Siddha and Sowa-Rigpa in these regulations (Annexure-VI) or
as amended from time to time.
(2) The standards and criteria mentioned for rating are over and above the minimum essential standards as
mentioned in these regulations; Rating process is intended for rating the fully established colleges or institutions
based on infrastructural standards, human resources and functionality over and above the minimum standards
requirements, and encouraging institutions to move towards higher standards in the area such as teaching, training,

| 80   |     |     |     |     |     |     |    [PART III—SEC.4]  |     |
| ---- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | -------------------- | --- |
THE GAZETTE OF INDIA : EXTRAORDINARY
human  resource  development,  healthcare  services,  research,  innovations,  co-curricular  or  extra-curricular
activities, new establishments, educational administration, education ecosystem etc.
(3) The fully established recognised colleges or institutions under section 28, fulfilling all Minimum Essential
Standard Requirements as mentioned in these regulations shall be eligible for rating; the college or institution,
which has been denied permission by the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine
National Commission for Indian System of Medicine or Government of India shall not be considered for rating for
the particular academic session.
(4) The newly established colleges under section 29, which are undergoing phase-wise establishment shall not be
considered eligible for rating, until they complete all four phase-wise establishments (first, second, third, fourth or
final) and annual targets as specified in regulation 13 of these regulations.
(5)  Calculation method for Rating of college or institution as follows:
(a) Key Indicators or Standards, Assessment criteria, Rating criteria, and Indicator wise-maximum score are
given in the column (B), (C), (D), and (E) respectively in the Annexure-V
(b) Each 01 point in the column (D) shall be considered as 01 score;
(c) Key indicator wise score (column D) to be converted to maximum 10 score (column E) and grand total
score obtained by the college or institution (column F) to be calculated;
(d) Conversion of total score into percentage of score, obtained by the College or institution shall be calculated
as follow;
|     |   Total score obtained.                |     |     |        |     |     |     |     |
| --- | -------------------------------------- | --- | --- | ------ | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|     |   -----------------------------------  |     |     | X 100  |     |     |     |     |
|     |   400 (Total maximum score)            |     |     |        |     |     |     |     |
(6)  Rating of the college or institution shall be awarded or granted as per the assessment outcome as shown in the
Table-5.
(7) The annual rating fee if any, apart from the visitation fee and digitisation fee as mentioned in these regulations
shall be fixed by the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine from time to time.
Table-5
 Total Score in Percentage, Status and Rating
| Score in percentage obtained  |     |     |     | Status.  |     |     | Rating.  |     |
| ----------------------------- | --- | --- | --- | -------- | --- | --- | -------- | --- |
by the College or Institution.     (Mulyankan or gnas tshad)
|     | (1)      |     |                                       | (2)  |     |     |     | (3)  |
| --- | -------- | --- | ------------------------------------- | ---- | --- | --- | --- | ---- |
|     | 81-100   |     | Uttam or phul byung or Excellent      |      |     |     |     | A    |
|     | 51-80    |     | Madhyam or legs or Good               |      |     |     |     | B    |
|     | Upto 50  |     | Santhoshjanak or dodlo khend tsam or  |      |     |     |     | C    |
Satisfactory
15.  Date  of  completion of  permission and  rating  process  and  cut-off-date for admission in Sowa-Rigpa
Colleges.- (1) The process of grant or denial of permission to the Sowa-Rigpa Medical Colleges or Institutions for
taking admissions and rating process shall be completed by the 30th June of each academic year or session.
(2) The cut-off-date for admission in Sowa-Rigpa colleges ordinarily be the 30th September of each academic
session or as specified by the National Commission for Indian System of Medicine from time to time.

Note: 1. The deficiency of teachers shall not exceed more than ten per cent. of total requirement with availability of
minimum one teacher in each of eight Departments for seeking conditional permission to undertake admission for
upcoming academic session (i.e. minimum eleven teaching staff for fifteen students intake capacity and sixteen for
thirty students intake capacity).
2. Wherever additional Professor or Associate Professor (Reader) are available in the Department, the additional
Professor or Associate Professor (Reader) shall be considered against the requirement of the Associate Professor
(Reader) or Assistant Professor (Lecturer) in the same Department.
3. Additional Professor or Associate Professor (Reader) or Assistant Professor (Lecturer) available in one Department,
shall not be counted or considered in the any other department where there is a shortage of faculty.

ESSENTIALITY CERTIFICATE OR NO OBJECTION CERTIFICATE
The Essentiality certificate or No Objection Certificate is issued to -------------------------------------------- (name of the
applicant) for the establishment of ------------------------------------- (name of the proposed college or institution)
at ------------------------------------------ (address of the proposed college or institution) with student intake capacity
of -------------- (Fifteen or Thirty). This certificate is issued in consideration of above details, facts, or conditions.
This certificate is valid for two consecutive academic sessions from the date of issue of the certificate.
The Essentiality Certificate or No Objection Certificate is issued on the following term and conditions:
1. College shall admit the students as per the sanctioned student intake capacity by the Medical Assessment and Rating Board
for Indian System of Medicine only after obtaining due permission from the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian
System of Medicine under National Commission for Indian System of Medicine.
2. College shall not conduct any other colleges, courses or programmes in the same premises unless otherwise permitted by the
Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine.
3. College shall maintain all the minimum essential standards in terms of infrastructure, human resources and functionality as
specified by the National Commission for Indian System of Medicine in accordance with student intake capacity.
4. College shall admit “National Commission for Indian System of Medicine-National Eligibility-cum-Entrance Test for Sowa-
Rigpa Under-Graduate” eligible students as per the extant regulations, guidelines and policies notified by the National
Commission for Indian System of Medicine.
5. The institution shall all times abide by the conditions laid down by the Autonomous Boards, National Commission for Indian
System of Medicine, Government of India, and University.
6. In case of change over the college to other society or trust, prior no objection certificate shall be obtained from the State
Government or Union territory Administration, as the case may be.
7. In case if the applicant fails to create or maintain infrastructure, human resources and other facilities for the Sowa-Rigpa
Medical College or Institution as per the minimum essential standards specified by the National Commission for Indian System
of Medicine, fresh admissions are stopped by the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine and the
University shall take over the responsibility of the students already admitted in the college with the permission of the Medical
Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine/National Commission for Indian System of Medicine.
8. In case of denial of permission or issued permanent disapproval to the college by the Medical Assessment and Rating Board
for Indian System of Medicine due to non-compliance of the college for minimum essential standards as prescribed by the
Commission, the State Government shall take over the responsibility of the students who have already been admitted in the
college with the permission of the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine.
(Signature of the Competent Authority)
Office Seal
Date:
Place:

1. College shall admit students as per the sanctioned student intake capacity by the Medical Assessment and
Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine only after obtaining due permission from the Medical Assessment
and Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine under National Commission for Indian System of Medicine.
2. College shall maintain all the minimum essential standards in terms of infrastructure, human resources and
functionality as specified by the National Commission for Indian System of Medicine in accordance with student
intake capacity.

Commission for Indian System of Medicine, Government of India and University.
5. In case if the applicant fails to create or maintain infrastructure, human resources and other facilities for the
Sowa-Rigpa Medical College or Institution as per the minimum essential standards specified by the National
Commission for Indian System of Medicine, fresh admissions are stopped by the Medical Assessment and Rating
Board for Indian System of Medicine and the University shall take over the responsibility of the students already
admitted in the college with the permission of the Medical Assessment and Rating Board for Indian System of
Medicine or National Commission for Indian System of Medicine.
6. In case of denial of permission or issued permanent disapproval to the college by the Medical Assessment and
Rating Board for Indian System of Medicine due to non-compliance of the college for minimum essential
standards as prescribed by the Commission, the State Government shall take over the responsibility of the students
who have already been admitted in the college with the permission of the Medical Assessment and Rating Board

THE GAZETTE OF INDIA : EXTRAORDINARY
CONSENT OF AFFILIATION

The university on the basis of local enquiry committee report, is agreed upon in principle to issue consent of affiliation
to---------------------------------------------------(name of the college) with  student intake capacity of  ------------------
(Fifteen or Thirty) seats of the proposed college or increase in number of seats or student intake capacity or admission
capacity from ---------------- to -------------- in already existing undergraduate programme.
The consent of affiliation is issued for the academic year(s)……………

Consent of affiliation is issued on the following terms and conditions:
1. The college shall maintain all the minimum essential standards in terms of infrastructure, human resources and functionality
as specified by the National Commission for Indian System of Medicine.
2. The college shall admit the “National Commission for Indian System of Medicine-National Eligibility-cum-Entrance Test for
Sowa-Rigpa Under-Graduate” eligible students through central counselling process as specified by the National Commission
for Indian System of Medicine in concerned regulations and guidelines.
3. The college shall ensure the conduction of stipulated hours of teaching and training as per the curriculum and syllabus
specified by the National Commission for Indian System of Medicine.
4. The colleges shall obtain continuation of affiliation every year at least three months before the commencement of admission
process.
5. Prior ‘No Objection Certificate’ shall be obtained from the present affiliating university in case of change of affiliation to
other university or applying for Deemed status.
6. In case of disaffiliation with the present university, the existing batches shall continue with the present university till award
of degree for the last student.
